3:56:4419:0:14:72:359:708:144:Times:144:Times:?:Agriculture, Roads, and Economic Development in Uganda
3:57:4473:14:14:72:256:694:144:Times:144:Times:?:Douglas Gollin and Richard Rogerson
3:58:4508:14:14:72:234:680:144:Times:144:Times:?:NBER Working Paper No. 15863
3:59:4536:14:14:72:130:666:144:Times:144:Times:?:March 2010

3:61:4572:28:42:273:338:624:144:Times:144:Times:A:ABSTRACT
3:62:4580:42:14:72:540:582:144:Times:144:Times:?:A  large  fraction  of  Uganda's  population  continues  to  earn  a  living  from  quasi-subsistence
3:63:4681:14:14:72:539:568:144:Times:144:Times:?:agriculture. This paper uses a static general equilibrium model to explore the relationships between
3:64:4781:14:14:72:540:554:144:Times:144:Times:?:high  transportation  costs,  low  productivity,  and  the  size  of  the  quasi-subsistence  sector.  We
3:65:4886:14:14:72:540:540:144:Times:144:Times:?:parameterize the model to replicate some key features of the Ugandan data, and we then perform a
3:66:4982:14:14:71:539:526:144:Times:144:Times:?:series  of  quantitative  experiments.  Our  results  suggest  that  the  population  in  quasi-subsistence
3:67:5089:14:14:71:539:512:144:Times:144:Times:?:agriculture is highly sensitive both to agricultural productivity levels and to transportation costs. The
3:68:5194:14:14:71:539:498:144:Times:144:Times:?:model also suggests positive complementarities between improvements in agricultural productivity
3:69:5290:14:42:71:161:484:144:Times:144:Times:?:and transportation.
